## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the classic setting for constitutive laws in thermoelasticity, plasticity, and high-temperature deformation where elastic moduli, yield/flow stress, and hardening/softening depend on T and epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Hooke (small-strain elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (isothermal linear elastic response)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermo-mechanical): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Polynomial-in-T modulus (higher-order thermoelasticity fit): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (captures curvature of E(T))
- Thermoelastic with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (free thermal expansion reduces mechanical strain)
- Elastic-perfectly-plastic style smooth cap (regularized yield): sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) (approximates yield saturation without a hard kink)
- Ludwik / Hollomon hardening (isothermal plastic hardening): sigma = c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2) ** c3 (work hardening with an offset to avoid singularity near 0)
- Ramberg–Osgood-like inverted form (empirical nonlinear elasticity/plasticity): sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1) ** c2 (nonlinear stress–strain curve as a power law)
- Combined linear + power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2) ** c3 (elastic + plastic contribution in a single expression)
- Thermal softening of strength (linear softening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2) ** c3) - c4 * T (yield/flow stress decreases with temperature)
- Multiplicative thermal softening (exponential): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2) ** c3) * exp(-c4 * T) (strength decays approximately exponentially with temperature)
- Johnson–Cook-like (strain hardening × thermal softening, no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon) + c2) ** c3) * (c4 - c5 * T) ** c6 (common metal plasticity structure with normalized thermal term)
- Entropic (rubber-like) elasticity using stretch lambda=1+epsilon: sigma = c0 * T * ((c1 + epsilon) - (c1 + epsilon) ** (-2)) (polymer network stress scales with absolute temperature and nonlinear stretch)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain linear regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; deviations indicate nonlinearity or onset of plasticity
- Thermal expansion appears as a strain shift → dependence on (epsilon - c * (T - T0)) rather than epsilon alone
- Elastic stiffness typically decreases with temperature → use E(T) multiplying epsilon where E(T) is linear/quadratic in T or decays with exp(-c*T)
- Plastic hardening often follows power-law in strain magnitude → (Abs(epsilon)+c)**n terms capture monotone hardening
- Yield/flow saturation (approaching a limiting stress) → tanh(c*epsilon) or rational-type saturation in epsilon
- Thermal softening is often multiplicative with hardening → [hardening(epsilon)] * [softening(T)] rather than additive mixing
- Tension/compression symmetry in scalar models → dependence on Abs(epsilon) when sign effects are not modeled
- Near glass transition or phase changes, stiffness/strength can drop rapidly → steep nonlinear E(T) (quadratic, exponential, or sharply varying softening factors)
- Polymer/rubber entropic stress scales with T → include an overall factor proportional to T in sigma when modeling elastomers

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
```
99.72829794207104*epsilon*(-0.08976441603442807*(T - 330.599841780566) + 1) + 4.818532892851478*epsilon**3 + 5.41673901332906*(T - 330.599841780566)*sin(epsilon)
```

Let me expand this:
- First term: `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*(T - 330.6) + 1)`
  = `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 0.08976...*330.6 + 1)`
  = `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 29.674... + 1)`
  = `99.728...*epsilon*(-0.08976...*T + 30.674...)`
  = `-8.951...*T*epsilon + 3059.4...*epsilon`

- Second term: `4.8185...*epsilon**3`

- Third term: `5.4167...*(T - 330.6)*sin(epsilon)`
  = `5.4167...*T*sin(epsilon) - 1790.8...*sin(epsilon)`

So GT = `-8.951*T*epsilon + 3059.4*epsilon + 4.8185*epsilon**3 + 5.4167*T*sin(epsilon) - 1790.8*sin(epsilon)`

The basis functions in GT are:
1. `T*epsilon` (linear coupling)
2. `epsilon` (linear)
3. `epsilon**3` (cubic)
4. `T*sin(epsilon)` (T times sin)
5. `sin(epsilon)` (pure sin)

Note: There's no pure `T` term, no constant term, and the sin argument is just `epsilon`.

Now let me check each candidate. The key structural requirements are:
- Must have `T*epsilon` term
- Must have `epsilon` term
- Must have `epsilon**3` term
- Must have `T*sin(epsilon)` term
- Must have `sin(epsilon)` term

The `T*sin(epsilon)` term is critical - it requires the sin term to be multiplied by T. Let me check which candidates can produce this.

Looking at the candidates, most have sin terms like `c*sin(c*epsilon + c)` without T multiplication. The GT requires `T*sin(epsilon)`, which means we need a term where T multiplies sin(epsilon).

Let me scan for candidates that can produce `T*sin(epsilon)`:

Most candidates have standalone `sin(c*epsilon + c)` terms without T multiplication. This means they CANNOT produce the `T*sin(epsilon)` term.

Let me check candidates that might have T-dependent sin terms or T multiplying sin:

- **Candidate 12**: Has `c2*sin(T*c3 + c4)` - this is sin of T, not T*sin(epsilon). NO.
- **Candidate 44**: Has `c6*epsilon*(T + c7)**c8` - this could give T*epsilon if c8=1, but not T*sin(epsilon).
- **Candidate 48**: `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*sin(c5*epsilon + c6)` - has T*epsilon but no T*sin(epsilon). Missing epsilon**3 too.
- **Candidate 54/55**: Similar issues.

None of the candidates have a `T*sin(epsilon)` term. The GT fundamentally requires this cross-term between T and sin(epsilon).

Let me verify this conclusion by checking every candidate systematically. Every candidate's sin terms are of the form `c*sin(c*epsilon + c)` without T multiplication, except Candidate 12 which has `sin(T*c3 + c4)` (wrong structure) and Candidate 57 which has `sin(T*c4 + c5)`.

Since no candidate can produce the `T*sin(epsilon)` basis function, none can match the GT.

Candidate 1-58 verdict: All [NO MATCH] due to missing `T*sin(epsilon)` term.
